Road Sweeper £30 2s. 2d. ,, 20th „ „ Geard, Mrs. Baths Attendant £9 18s. 4d. „ 29 REPORT OF THE COUNCIL of the METROPOLITAN BOROUGH OF WANDSWORTH For the Year ended 31st March, 1912. 1. At the Meeting of the Council on the 9th November, Election of Mayor. 1911, Alderman Archibald Davis Dawnay, J.P., was unanimously re-elected Mayor of the Borough. The Council at its Meeting on the 18th October, 1911, resolved unanimously:— Address to the Mayor. "That the best thanks of the Council be presented to Alderman Archibald Davis Dawnay, J.P., for his able, courteous, and impartial conduct in the Chair, and for the time and attention bestowed by him in the discharge of his duties as Mayor of this Borough for the third year in succession." 3. The General Purposes Committee were instructed to prepare and settle an Address expressing the Council's high appreciation of Alderman Dawnay's services. 4. The following Address was accordingly engrossed, framed, sealed with the Common Seal of the Council and presented to Alderman Dawnay at the Meeting of the Council on the 9th November:— 30 METROPOLITAN BOROUGH OF WANDSWORTH. Population. Area. Rateable Value. 311,402. 9,199 acres. £2,155,122. To Alderman Archibald Davis Dawnay, J.P. We, the Aldermen and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth, hereby express our high appreciation of your valuable services as Mayor during the year November, 1910—November. 1911, being the third successive year in which you have served that Office. The past year has been memorable as being that of the Coronation of Their Majesties King George V. and Queen Mary. In connection therewith it was your duty and privilege to be in attendance on the 22nd June at Ihe Coronation in Westminster Abbey; and on the following day, in company with the nine other Mayors of South London Boroughs, to present to their Majesties a combined Loyal Address from those Boroughs on the occasion of the Royal Progress through I.ondon. We recall the arduous labours which you undertook in arranging for the Public Entertainments and Festivities given to 51,000 children in this Borough in celebration of Their Majesties' Coronation, at one of which, held in the grounds adjoining the Royal Hospital for Incurables at West Hill, Wandsworth, you had the distinguished honour of receiving Their Royal Highnesses the Duke and Duchess of Connaught, who gave to the children there assembled gracious messages from Their Majesties. These festivities were rendered particularly memorable by the specially struck Coronation Medals which you generously presented to the Council, to its Members, to the children and to man}' other inhabitants of the Borough. It is with great pleasure that we are able to congratulate you upon the success of your appeal for public subscriptions for the Borough of Wandsworth Memorial Statue to His late Majesty King Edward VII., which has been recently erected at Tooting Broadway. We must also allude to the enterprise shown by you in the establishment of the Inter-Borough Rifle Contest, which has had the effect of greatly stimulating the interest taken in Miniature Rifle Shooting, and has brought about most pleasant social relations between the residents in the several Boroughs in and near the Metropolis. The handsome Challenge Cup, generously provided by you, was appropriately won in the first year's contest by the Team from this Borough. In all the matters to which we have referred, and on the numerous other occasions when you have represented this Borough, you have most worthily upheld the dignity and importance of the high position to which you were unanimously re-elected by us a year ago, and we acknowledge with gratitude the very zealous and successful manner in which the heavy and important duties of your Office have been discharged, and the generous hospitalitv extended by you to all classes and to every part of the Borough. 31 We also record our heartiest thanks to the Mayoress for the kindly and gracious manner in which she has supported you in your many Social and Public Undertakings, and we trust that the events of the year and of your two preceding years of Office will ever remain in your memories a bright and interesting recollection. SEALED by Order this ist day of November, ign. (Signed) J. W. LORDF.N, Ex Mayer. L.S. (Signed) HEN. GEO. HILLS, Town Clerk. 9th November, 1911. Presentation to the Mayor. 5. Alderman Lorden, L.C.C., on behalf of the subscribers (members and ex-members of the Council) presented to the Mayor his portrait in oils, painted by Mr. C. E. Butler, and a replica thereof by the same artist. The portrait having been unveiled by Alderman Lorden, the Mayor thanked the subscribers and presented one of the portraits to the Council. Alderman Lorden accepted the portrait on behalf of the Council, and it is now hung in the Council Chamber. Presentation to the Mayoress. 6. On the same occasion Councillor Lieut.-General Sir Frederick Lance, K.C.B., on behalf of the subscribers, presented to Mrs. Dawnay a gold and platinum watch bracelet with the Borough Arms engraved on the watch case and an inscription on the dome, as a mark of appreciation of her services in the discharge of the duties of Mayoress during the past year. Resignation of Councillors. 7. Councillor Turnbull, member for the Balham Ward, and Councillor Gosden, member for the Putney Ward, resigned their offices of Councillor on the 17th August and 18th October respectively. Casual Vacancies. 8. The vacancy in the Balham Ward caused by the resignation of Councillor Turnbull was filled by the election of Dr. Marcus Glanville. No poll was necessary, only one nomination being received. The vacancy in the Putney Ward was filled by the election of Mr. A. Cooper Rawson. The election was held on the 14th November, when the votes recorded were as follows:— Names of Candidates. No. of Votes recorded. Rawson, Alfred Cooper 1,664 (elected) Waiters, Frank 283 32 9. The number of electors, the number of electors voting, &c.,. were as follows, viz.;— Number of Electors. Number of Electors voting. Percentage of Electors voting. Number of rejected Ballot Papers. 5,691 1,948 34.23 I Church Services. 10. The Mayor, Aldermen, Councillors, and principal officers. of the Council, attended in State services at the following churches in the Borough, viz.:— 14th May, 1911 Parish Church, of Tooting, St. Nicholas, Church Lane. nth February, 1912 Parish Church of Putney, St. Mary, High Street. 11. The Council also attended in State, on the 5th November, 1911, a Municipal Service at Southwark Cathedral. Putney Charities. 12. Councillor Radford was re-appointed for a period of four years from the 4th October, 1911, to act in the administration of the following charities:—Henry Smith, Sir Abraham Dawe's Almhouses, and Benjamin Hunt Bigg. Wandsworth Charities. 13. Alderman Robinson, a Representative Trustee of the Wandsworth Consolidated Charities for the Fairfield Ward, was re-appointed a Representative. Trustee of such Charities for the Fairfield Ward for a period of four years from the 18th December, 1911. 14. Admiral Campbell having resigned his appointment as Representative Trustee of the Wandsworth Consolidated Charities for the Southfield Ward, Councillor Webster Jones was appointed a Representative Trustee of such Charities for the Southfield Ward for a period of four years from the 24th January, 1912. Streatham Charities. 15. The period for which Councillor Nutting was appointed a Representative Trustee of the Streatham NonEcclesiastical Charities having expired, Councillor Nutting was re-appointed a Representative Trustee of such Charities for a period of four years from the 7th February, 1912. Summertown Educational Foundation. 16. The period for which Alderman Cresswell was appointed a Representative Trustee of the Summerstown Educational Foundation having expired, Alderman Cresswell was re-appointed a Representative Trustee of such Foundation for a pericd of threeyears from the 6th March, 1912. 33 Wandsworth Technical Institute. 17. The vacancy on the Governing Body of the Wandsworth. Technical Institute caused by the expiration of the period for which Mr. A. J. Littlechild was appointed was filled by re-appointing Mr. Littlechild on the Governing Body of such Institute for a period of three years from the 31st July, 1911. Thomas IVartyn's Foundation (otherwise the Waterman's School). 18. The Scheme for the administration of the Thomas Martyn's Foundation (otherwise the Waterman's School, Putney), approved by Order in Council on the 3rd October, 1911, provides that two Representative Governors shall be appointed by the Borough Council. Councillors Mathias and Renshaw were appointed the Council's representatives on the Governing Body of the Foundation for a period of three years from the 18th October, 1911. Clapham Charities. 19. The Scheme for the administration of the Edward Baker (Clapham) Charity provides that at the end of two years from the 10th December, 1909, one of the three Representative Trustees appointed by the Council shall go out of office, but shall be eligible for re-election. The Mayor (Alderman Archibald D. Dawnay) went out of office on the 10th December last, and was re-appointed a Representative Trustee for a period of four years from that date. Coronation. 20. The Council appointed the Mayor, Aldermen Hunt, J.P., L.C.C., and Lorden, L.C.C., and Councillors Anderson, M.A., Campbell, C. B., Sir Frederick Lance, K.C.B., and Wise, a Committee to consider and report what steps should be taken by the Council on behalf of the Borough to commemorate the Coronation of their Majesties King George V. and Queen Mary. 21. It was finally dccidcd that the Coronation should be celebrated in the Borough by entertaining all children attending public elementary schools (including the non-provided schools) in the Borough. A separate Committee consisting of the Aldermen and Members of the Council, School Managers and Teachers, and others in the respective Wards, was appointed for each Ward (the Fairfield and Southfield Wards afterwards combining) to make all arrangements for the entertainments, including settling terms with caterers, amusements, use of tents, schoolrooms, and all other requirements. 34 22. The arrangements for the entertainment of the children attending the East Wandsworth and West Wandsworth Special Schools were undertaken, on behalf of the Committee, by the. respective Bodies of Managers of those Schools. 23. The entertainments took the form of a tea, games, music, etc., in schools and open spaces. 24. Their Royal Highnesses the Duke and Duchess of Connaught attended the entertainment given to the children of the Fairfield and Southfield Wards in the grounds of the Royal Hospital for Incurables and the Leg of Mutton Field, Southfield, on Monday, the 26th June, and were received by the Mayor and Mayoress and the Town Clerk, Sir Henry Kimber, Bart., M.P., the Bishop of Southwark, Aldermen and Councillors of the Borough, and members of the Hospital Board of Management. Their Royal Highnesses were very much interested in the entertainments and the singing of the children, and their visit was highly appreciated by the •children. Most of the other entertainments were visited by the Mayor and Mayoress and the Town Clerk. 25. The Mayor presented a Coronation Medal in a case to each Ward Committee for a prize for a race for boys, and sent handsome invitation cards to the children and helpers in the Clapham North Ward. The Mayor also gave a Coronation Medal to the top boy and a Coronation Brooch to the top girl in each class of the Public Elementary Schools, and Sir Henry Kimber gave Coronation Medals to infants. Many other prizes and gifts were kindly presented by ladies and gentlemen and associations who took an interest in the celebrations in the different Wards. 26. The respective Ward Committees made efficient arrangements for the entertainments, and they were carried out in a very satisfactory manner. The thanks of the Council were accorded to the Members of the Committees and other ladies and gentlemen, and especially to the teachers, for the great time given and trouble taken to make the entertainments a thorough success. 27. The Council House, Town Hall, the several public libraries, the Rating and Registration Offices, the Borough Engineer's Offices, and the Tooting and Wandsworth Baths, were illuminated on the 22nd, 23rd, 26th, and 27th June; and many of the tradesmen and others kept up the decorations and illuminations which they had used on Coronation Day. 29. Subscriptions amounting to £737 8s. 5d. were received from residents towards the cost of the celebration, the total cost of which was £2,362 14s. 0d. 30. The following Parliamentary Bills were considered by the Council, viz.:— London County Council (General Powers). Metropolitan District Railway. Wandsworth, Wimbledon and Epsom District Gas. Music and Dancing Licences. Daylight Saving. National Insurance. Parliamentary Franchise (Women). Rag Flock. Representation of the People. Shops. Aliens (Prevention of Crime). London County Council (Finance). Aliens. Disorderly Houses. Parliamentary Elections. Poor Law (London). Summer Season (Daylight Saving). L.C.C. (Gencral Powers.) 31. Part III. of this Bill proposed to authorize the London County Council to hold, lay out, and develop on the lines of a garden suburb part of the White Hart estate, Tottenham, and to let plots of land on lease for buildings other than for the accommodation of the working classes. This Council saw no objection to the London County Council disposing of part of the estate but was of opinion that such Council should not be empowered to build premises other than for the accommodation of the working classes on the estate. The Bjll rectived Royal Ascent on the 7th August, 1912. 37 Metropolitan District Railway Bill. 32. This Bill proposed to authorize the South Western Railway Company to widen the Wimbledon and Fulham Railway and works, and for that purpose to purchase certain premises in this Borough and to interfere with highways and rights and powers of the Council. A petition was presented against the Bill and clauses for the protection of this Borough having been agreed, the Council's opposition was withdrawn, and the Bill received the Royal Assent on the 7th August, 1912. Wandsworth, Wimbledon, and Epsom District Gas Bill. 33. The object of this Bill was to constitute as one undertaking the undertakings of the Wandsworth & Putney, the Mitcham & Wimbledon, and the Epsom & Ewell Gas Companies. With the exception of a few minor matters no new powers were sought. The total capital of the new company is the sum of the total capital of the three Companies. The Bill proposed to authorise the Company to exercise the powers conferred upon the Wandsworth Gas Co., in 1900, to stop up certain footpaths and thoroughfares in this Borough. The Bill also provided for the then standard price of gas to be continued. The Council presented a petition against the Bill with the view of obtaining the insertion of clauses for the protection of this Borough. The Company afterwards agreed to insert clauses providing for penalties in respect of calorific tests in lieu of those for illuminating power, for the provision of a second testing place in the Wandsworth limit, and with respect to the relative prices of gas in the several limits, and other matters, whereupon the Council's opposition was withdrawn, and the Bill received Royal Assent on the 7th August. Music and Dancing. 34. This Bill was to the same effect as the Bill referred to in paragraph 44 of the Council's last Annual Report. The Council petitioned in favour thereof. The Bill was read a third time in the House of Lords and then dropped. Metropolitan Police Rate. 35. This Bill proposed to increase the maximum of the Police Rate from gd. to nd. in the £. The Council presented a petition against the Bill, which, however, received Royal Assent on the 29th March, 1912. 38 Daylight Saving Bill. 36. This Council presented a petition in favour of this Biil and also forwarded a copy of a resolution in favour thereof to His Majesty's Government and also to the leader of the Opposition. The Bill was not proceeded with. National Health Insurance. 37. The Council presented a petition against this Bill objecting to the creation of Local Health Committees as proposed, to the provisions relating to contributions of employers towards the insurance of workmen on the ground that such contributions should fall upon the State, to the provisions relating to voluntary contributions, and generally on the ground that the Bill was being pushed forward with undue haste. The Bill received Royal Assent on the 16th December, 1911. Parliamentary Franchise of Women. 38. The Council asked the Members of Parliament for this Borough to support facilities being afforded for the consideration of this Bill. Rag Flock. 39. The Council suggested two amendments to this Bill which, however, were not adopted, and the Bill received Royal Assent on the 16th December, 1911. Representation of the people. 40. This Bill was again introduced by Sir Henry Kimber, Bart., M.P., its object being to make the representation in the House of Commons more nearly proportionate to population. The Council petitioned in favour of the measure,, but the Bill did not reach the second reading. Shops Bill. 41. The Council presented a petition against this Bill on the ground that its provisions were an undue interference with trade. The Bill received Royal Assent on the 16th December, 1911. Aliens Prevention of Crime. 42 The Council presented a petition in favour of this Bill which was dropped. 43. No order was made with regard to the other Bills abovementioned. 39 Memorial to King Edward VII. 44. In continuation of our last Annual Report (page 36) we have to report that the Borough Memorial to His late Majesty King Edward VII., at Tooting Broadway, was unveiled by the Mayor on the 4th November, and the following is a copy of a telegram sent to the King on the occasion, and of His Majesty's reply; viz.:— "To His Gracious Majesty The King, Sandringham. "May it please your Majesty. We have this clay unveiled, at Tooting Broadway, in the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth, a noble statue to His late Majesty King Edward VII. Your devoted subjects here humbly bid you and Her Majesty God speed on your visit to India, and a safe and happy return home. "The Mayor, Wandsworth." "To The Mayor, Wandsworth. "The King is much gratified to hear that you have to-day unveiled a statue to King Edward, which the people of Wandsworth have erectcd to his dear memory. His Majesty sincerely thanks you and those who join with you for the kind sentiments and good wishes to which your telegram gives expression. "C. Wigram." 45. The Memorial consists of a bronze statue of His late Majesty King Edward VII. in regal robes, seven feet six inches in height, standing upon a pedestal of polished red granite nine feet four inches in height. The pedestal bears the following inscription, viz.:— EDWARD VII. and on the lower plinth in front:— Erected by Public Subscription. 1911. Alderman Archibald Davis Dawnay, J.P., Mayor. The sculptor is Mr. Louis Fritz Roselieb, of Clapham. 46. Mounted and bound photographs of the Statue were forwarded to His Majesty King George V., and to Her Majesty Queen Alexandra. 47. The Committee who had the matter in hand expressed their entire satisfaction with the Memorial, and the subscriptions received were sufficient to meet the expenses. C 40 Royal Patriotic Asylum. 48. The Royal Patriotic Fund Corporation having proposed to dispose of about 20 acres of land adjoining the Royal Victoria Patriotic Asylum at Wandsworth Common, the Council, in view of the fact that the land formerly formed part of Wandsworth Common, strongly objected to its being used for any other purpose than an open space, and deputations from this Council and the Battersea Borough Council in support of this Council's views attended before the Parks and Open Spaces Committee of the London County Council in support of the land in question being acquired and added to Wandsworth Common. 49. The Mayor convened a Towns Meeting at the Town Hall on the 28th October, when the following resolutions were passed, viz.:— "(1) This Meeting of the inhabitants of Wandsworth and Battersea deplores the Royal Patriotic Corporation's proposal to dispose (possibly for building purposes) of the 20 acres of land, known as 'The Farm,' formerly a part of Wandsworth Common, and held as 'a visible and permanent memorial of the national generosity.' "(2) This Meeting urges upon the London County Council and the Borough Councils of Wandsworth and Battersea the necessity of taking immediate and at the same time reasonable and equitable measures for the preservation of the land as an open space. "(3) That the Chairman of this Meeting (Alderman Archibald D. Dawnay, J.P., Mayor of Wandsworth), be authorised to sign and transmit copies of the above resolutions to the London County Council, the Wandsworth and Battersea Borough Councils, the President of the Local Government Board, and the local Members of Parliament; that a Deputation be appointed to wait upon the Royal Patriotic Corporation and present the Resolutions to them; and that the Deputation consist of the speakers this evening and the two honorary secretaries of the Wandsworth Common Protection Association. (4) That the Deputation appointed this evening be requested to take steps with the view of raising a Fund towards the acquisition of the land." 50. The estimated cost of purchasing the land was about £12,000 and this Council asked the London County Council to acquire the land for use as an open space, and agreed to contribute £3,000 towards the cost, provided that a similar sum was contributed by the Battersea Borough Council and public subscription. The County Council adopted the suggestion and the agreement with the London County Council for payment of this Council's contribution was sealed by the Council on the 20th January, 1912. 41 Metropolitan Borough's Standing Joint Committee. 51. A Standing Joint Committee of representatives of the Metropolitan City and Borough Councils having been formed to watch over and take steps for safeguarding the rights, authority, interests and duties of such Councils as they may bs affected by legislation or otherwise, and to confer and advise upon matters of common interest generally, the Mayor, Alderman Linclsey and the Town Clerk, were appointed this Council's representatives on such Committee. The Mayor was subsequently elected a member of the Executive Committee. National Reserve. S2. The Council decided to form a National Reserve Committee for this Borough, consisting of the Mayor, Aldermen Cresswell, Lindsey and Surgeon Major Robinson, I.M.D., Councillors Campbell, C.B., Cundall and Sir Frederick Lance, K.C.B, and Members of. the Wandsworth Military Committee, with such additional members as might be considered desirable. Town Clerk. 53. Mr. H. G. Hills, who had been Town Clerk of the Borough since the beginning of the Council, having resigned his appointment, the Council presented him with the following illuminated address, viz.:— METROPOLITAN BOROUGH OF WANDSWORTH. Area, 9,199 acres. Population in 1900 232,032. Population in 1912 311,482. Rateable Value £1,527,029. Rateable Value £2,124,213, To Henry George Hills, Esquire. We, the Mayor, Aldermen, and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth, in regretfully accepting your resignation of the office of Town Clerk of this Borough, desire to place on record our great appreciation of your long and distinguished services, not only to this Borough since it was created in 1900, when you were unanimously appointed Town Clerk, but also of the Wandsworth District Board of Works, which preceded this Borough, and of which you were the Assistant Clerk for nine years, and also Clerk for nearly sixteen years. Some Members of the Council were members of the District Board, and from their testimony we are pleased to say that you discharged your duties of Clerk to that Board in a most efficient manner, and that it was under many and great obligations to you for the indefatigable assistance you rendered on the passing of the Act of Parliament for separating the Parish of Battersea from the other Territory of the Board. 42 It is with much pleasure we express how highly we value your able advice and guidance in settling the transfer of the officers of the District Board and the division of assets between the two Boards. Your services also to the New Borough when it was formed were of the greatest possible aid to the Council in making the numerous arrangements which became necessary under the provisions of the London Government Act of 1899, and more especially in effecting a uniformity of Rating and administration throughout this Borough, and in the amalgamation of the five ancient Parishes of Clapham, Putney, Streatham, Tooting, and Wandsworth into one civil Parish; and from that time to the present you have continued to carry out your multifarious duties, official and social, in a most assiduous and genial manner, thereby not only winning the admiration of the Count il but of everyone whom you have had to meet in the pursuit of your offkial calling. The notable fact that you were elected Chairman of the Metropolitan Association of Town Clerks is a most valuable testimony to your great experience and ability, and proves how highly you were esteemed by that important body. We must also record that during your office two beloved Sovereigns passed away—Their late Majesties Queen Victoria and King Edward VII—and that you were instructed to prepare the Addresses to the Throne on their demise, and also on the occasion of the accession of His late Majesty King Edward VII and His present Majesty King Ceorge V; and that you represented this Borough, with the Mayor and other Members of the Council, at the presentation of the Addresses to Their Majesties. We also gratefully acknowledge the ungrudging and kind assistance rendered by you in connection with the festivities held in this Borough at the Coronation of both the Kings and Oueens. The Council expresses its sincere regret in losing your faithful and valuable services, and assures you that in your well-earned retirement you will take with you the highest esteem and respect not onlv of every member of the Council, but also of every ratepayer in this Borough, and we give expression to the earnest hope that Mrs. Hills and yourself will be spared with The Almighty's blessing for the peaceful enjoyment of many years to come. Sealed by Order, this 24th day of April, 1912. (Signed) ARCHIBALD D. DAWNAY, Mayor. (L.S.) (Signed) D. A. NICHOLL, Town Clerk. 54. To fill the vacancy caused by the retirement of Mr. Hills, the Council, at its meeting on the 21st February, 1912, appointed Mr. David Arthur Nicholl, M.A., LL.M. (Carnb.), Town Clerk of Scarborough, Town Clerk of the Borough of Wandsworth. Metropolitan Paving Committee. 55. Alderman Hewett, J.P., has again been appointed as this Council's representative on the Metropolitan Paving Committee. Motor Omnibus Traffic. 56. A conference of Metropolitan, City and Borough Councils, on the subject of motor omnibus traffic in London, convened by the Hampstead Borough Council, was 43 held at Westminster City Hall on 6th February last, when Councillors Jackson and Plumridge, and the Town Clerk, attended as this Council's representatives, and resolutions were passed in favour of proprietors of mechanically-propelled vehicles in London being brought under contribution for the repair and upkeep of roads used by such vehicles, and of further measures being taken for the control of motor omnibus traffic. 57. The Borough Council has since urged the Government to introduce legislation establishing a Traffic Board for the regulation of vehicular traffic in London, and providing for the distribution of the proceeds of the petrol tax received from the County of London among the Metropolitan Borough Councils as a contribution towards the maintenance of highways Speed Limit for Motor Traffic. 58. At the suggestion of the Borough Council, theTondon County Council applied to the Local Government Board for a regulation to be made prescribing a maximum speed not exceeeling 10 miles an hour for motor vehicles on Putney Bridge and in High Street, Putney. The Borough Council supported the proposal at the Local Inquiry held by the Board recently, and the application has now been granted and the necessary order made by the Board. The usual notices have been fixed in the area affected. 59. Applications were also made by the London County Council to the Local Government Board for regulations to be made reducing the speed limit for motor traffic in the following thoroughfares in the Borough, viz.:— (a) Streatham High Road, from Pinfold Road to Stan- thorpe Road. (b) footing Bee Gardens, from Ambleside Avenue to Streatham High Road. (c) Clapham Common South Side, from Cavendish Road to Balham Hill. (d) Balham Hill, from Clapham Common to Balham High Road. (e) Balham High Road, from Balham Hill to Balham Park Road. (f) Upper Tooting Road, from Tooting Bee Road to Tooting High Street. (g) Tooting High Street, from Upper Tooting Road to Tooting Graveney School. 44 6o. After careful consideration of all the circumstances, the Borough Council came to the conclusion that it was not desirable that any reduction should be made in the speed limit in these thoroughfares; and the London County Council and Local Government Board were so informed. A Local Government Board Inquiry was held with regard to the Streatham High Road and Tooting Bee Gardens proposals, and after considering the report of their Inspector the Board decided not to comply with the application in those cases. Putney to Wandsworth. Tramways. 61. The construction of the tramways in the portion of this route between Putney Bridge and the junction of Putney Bridge Road with High Street, Wandsworth, has been completed. The line was inspected on behalf of the Board of Trade on 26th January, 1912, and was shortly afterwards opened for traffic. 62. The Borough Council has been in communication with the County Council with regard to additional widenings which are required in Putney Bridge Road and the County Council has promised to bear the suggestions in mind when favourable opportunities offer. 63. Steps are being taken by the London County Council for widening High Street, Wandsworth, so as to allow of the extension of the line along that thoroughfare to join up with the existing tramways in York Road. With the view of assisting the County Council to effect the improvement without delay the Borough Council agreed to give up the part of the forecourt of the Wandsworth Public Baths required to be added to the public way there. Arrangements have also been made for widening the bridge over the river Wandle, and this work will be begun shortly. 64. The Borough Council asked the London County Council to extend the widening at and near the corner of High Street, Putney, and Putney Bridge Road, so as to include the part of the road in front of Nos. 17, 19, 21 and 25, High Street, Putney, if the necessary property could be obtained at a reasonable cost. The County Council adopted the suggestion with regard to No. 25, High Street, Putney, and continued the widening in front of those 45 premises, tlie expenditure being covered by the estimate in respect of the general widening of Putney Bridge Road, towards the cost of which the Borough Council is contributing one-third. Cedars Road and Southcroft Road Woodpaving. 65. Under agreements between the Borough Council and the County Council, the periods within which the Borough Council was to pave with wood the carriageways (excluding the tramway tracks and margins) of parts of Cedars Road, Clapham, and Southcroft Road, Streatham, were extended by eighteen months in each case. East Hill Widening. 66. A widening of East Hill, between Fairfield Street and the Baptist Chapel, has been carried out by the London County Council, the Borough Council contributing one-third of the expense. The estimated cost was £2,360. High Street, Wandsworth and St. Ann's Hill Widening. 67. In accordance with the terms of the agreement between the Borough Council and the County Council referred to in a previous report, the County Council gave up the strip of the site of the Old Vicarage, in high street, wandsworth, required for widening the public way there to 54 feet, and the Borough Council continued the widening to the foot of St. Ann's Hill. At the time when the agreement was entered into the County Council proposed to erect a new technical institute at the junction of High Street, Wandsworth, and St. Ann's Hill. The Borough Council has on many occasions urged upon the County Council the desirability of the scheme being proceeded with, and on 12th June, 1912, a deputation, consisting of the Mayor, Aldermen Cresswell and Penfold, Councillors Bulstrode, Denny, Harding, and Plumridge, attended before the Higher Education Sub-Committee of the County Council in support of the proposal. The matter is still under the consideration of the County Council. York Road Widening. 68. The widening of York Road, Wandsworth, by the Borough Council is now almost complete. The Council has, however, been unable to agree reasonable terms for certain outstanding interests, and steps are being taken for their compulsory purchase under Michael Angelo Taylor's Act. 46 Bridge over Hailway, High Street, Putney. 69. The London and South-Western Railway Company having stated their intention to reconstruct at an early date a section of the bridge carrying High Street, Putney, over the railway, a scheme has been prepared by the Company's Engineer in collaboration with the Engineer to the Metropolitan Water Board and the Borough Engineer for widening the bridge and for placing the Water Board's mains under the public way in lieu of their being carried alongside the bridge as at present. The Borough Council is now in communication with the Road Board, the London County Council, and the Railway Company with the view of those bodies contributing towards the cost of the proposed works. Upper Richmond Road Improvement. 70. The Barnes Urban District Council and the London County Council having considered the Borough Council's suggestion as to the improvement of Upper Rich- mond road, putney, at the County boundary near Priests' Bridge, agreed to support an application to the Road Board in favour of the scheme, but were not prepared to make any contribution towards the cost. As these authorities declined to give the proposal their financial support, the Borough Council did not feel justified in proceeding further with the matter. 71. The part of Upper Richmond Road, between Priory Lane and the County boundary at Priests' Bridge, has since been paved with the following materials as an experiment, viz.:—(a) Cormastik road material; (b) Durax armouring, part Enderby and part Norway granite; and (c) granite macadam with Plascom binding material. In connection with the formation of new roads (Montana Road and Avoca Road), on the Elmwood House Estate, Balham, and the erection of houses there, arrangements were made for parts of Tooting Bee Road upon which the estate abuts to be widened to not less than 54 feet. This condition was accepted by the Borough Council, provided its contribution did not exceed £483. Tooting Bec Gardens Widening. 76. The London County Council is contributing one-half the net cost of this further widening. Streatham High Road. 77. For several years past the Borough Council has been pressing the London County Council for consent to form a footpath at the side of Streatham Common adjoining Streatham High Road and to round off the corners of the Common at the junction of that road with Streatham Common North and Streatham Common South. The approval of the County Council to these works has now been obtained. The scheme provides for the formation of a tar-dressed footpath with granite kerb, alongside the carriageway in Streatham High Road, the estimated cost being £265. 48 78. In connection with the rebuilding of the Police Station at the corner of Streatham High Road and Shrubbery Road, the London County Council arranged for the main road to be widened to 60 feet, the Borough Council contributing one-third of the net cost of the improvement, which was estimated at £300. 79. By agreement with the owners of the Crooke Ellison Estate, land on both sides of Greyhound Lane, Streatham, was required to be given up for the purpose of widening that road. In pursuance of this agreement a strip of land on the north-western side of the Lane was added to the public way after being levelled and covered with ashes, spur stones being placed alongside the carriageway where necessary. The Borough Council also took possession of a piece of land on the south-eastern side of the road, and fixed spur stones on the new boundary at the back of the hedge and bank, which it is proposed should remain for the present. This hedge and bank can be removed and the land levelled at any time the Council thinks fit. Greyhound Lane Widening. 80. Tooting Gardens. 87. The Council had under consideiation during the past year the question of improving the public lighting of the streets in the Borough. After correspondence with the various gas companies, arrangements were made for a Lighting. 49 50 number of upright incandescent burners to be converted into inverted burners and for the number of lighting hours to be made practically uniform throughout the Borough. Although the streets will be better lighted, the cost per lamp per annum will be reduced after the first year, when the cost of the alterations has to be borne. With reference to the suggested adoption of high-pressure gas lighting in some of the main roads, the Council decided that, in view of the cost, it was not advisable to take any action at present. It has recently been arranged for a trial to be made of two-burner inverted lamps in one of the main roads, and the question of further improving the lighting of the public streets will continue to receive the attention of the Council. 88. The Borough Council has for several years past been in communication with the London County Council with regard to the flooding which takes place in some parts of the Borough during heavy rainstorms. A certain measure of relief was afforded by the new sewer from Wandsworth to Battersea recently constructed by the County Council, but on the occasion of the severe storms in August, 1911, there was a considerable amount of flooding in several localities. A number of complaints were received, and as the Borough Council felt that immediate action should be taken to provide adequate main sewers to cope with the drainage of the district, a deputation, consisting of the Mayor (Alderman A. D. Dawnay, J.P.), Councillors Garrett and Jackson (Chairman and Vice-Chairman of the Highways, Sewers, and Lighting Committee), Aldermen Hewett, J.P., and Penfold, Councillors Doland, Eaton, Nutting, and Plumridge, was appointed to wait upon the County Council on the subject. The deputation was received by the Main Drainage Committee of the County Council on 26th October, 1911, when there were also in attendance deputations from some of the districts affected. The Mayor acted as spokesman for the Borough Council deputation, and urged the Committee to take prompt measures for the relief of the Borough from the liability to floodings from which it had suffered in the past. The representations of the deputations having been considered by the Main Drainage Committee, the County Council, on 7th November, 1911, upon their recommendation, decided to undertake the following works, viz.:— Flooding from Sewers. 51 Estimated cost. (1) A relief sewer from the junction of Balham High Road and Tooting Bee Road to the river Graveney £28,000 (2) Improvement of the waterway of the river Graveney— (a) from its junction with the proposed new sewer to the river Wandle 4,000 (b) near and under Longley Road 1,750 £33.750 89. It is anticipated that these works will prevent flooding from the sewers in the districts around Balham Park Road and Mayford Road, Balham, and at the eastern end of Longley Road, Tooting. .90. More recently the County Council approved an estimate of £100,000 for the construction of a new sewer to prevent flooding in the low-lying areas in the valley of the rivers Wandle and Graveney. The proposed works are in addition to those referred to above and are expected to suffice for the needs of the district for many years. 91. Swimming competitions for school children were held at the Wandsworth Baths on the 13th October, and a free pass to the second-class bath, available during the following year, was awarded to the successful boy or girl from each school. The competitions are open to boys and girls from schools in the Borough attending the baths for instruction in swimming, the passes are available out of school hours before seven o'clock in the evening. A large number of children and their parents were present. All the departments of elementary schools sending pupils to the baths for instruction in swimming entered pupils for the competitions. The number of children taking part in the competitions was 167—97 boys and 70 girls. Swimming Comoetitions for School Children. 94. Difficulty having been experienced in drying the towels, &c., in the laundry at the Wandsworth Baths, alterations and additions have been carried out in order to make the machinery more efficient. The drying closet has been extended by the addition of six new horses, the heater replaced by one of larger heating surface and capable of standing a higher pressure, and a new blower of higher speed provided. A new fan and shaft for ventilating the laundry has also been provided. Wandsworth Baths. —Laundry. 97. Exceeding one month, but not exceeding six years 11/- 18/- 9/- 14/- Exceeding six years, but not exceeding twelve years 14/- 24 /- 12 /- 20/- Exceeding twelve years 18/- 3 2/- 1 26/— 55 103- On the instructions of the Council the Cemeteries Committee considered the subject of laying out additional land for burials at Putney Vale Cemetery. Before the preparation of a scheme for this purpose it was thought desirable to consider whether further land was required. There is considerable demand for the highest priced spaces in the cemetery, and the Committee considered it would be a great advantage to the cemetery if the high land adjoining Wimbledon Common, and situate between the cemetery and Stag Lane, could be acquired, with the view of providing spaces of this description, and for which it was eminently suitable. The Council adopted this view, and after negotiation with the owners decided, subject to the approval of the Local Government Board, to purchase an area of 29 acres, 3 roods, 2 poles at the price of £350 per acre. The Board held a public enquiry into the Council's proposal, and on the 3rd April, 1912, formally approved the purchase, and sanctioned a loan therefor. Steps are being taken to redeem the tithe rent charge payable on this and other land belonging to the Council at Putney Vale. 104. With regard to the laying out of the land the Council decided to retain the services of Mr. Thomas H. Mawson, a landscape architect who has had considerable experience in this kind of work, to prepare plans and designs, and to give an estimate of the cost of tree planting. The Borough Engineer is also preparing an estimate of the cost of drainage, formation of walks and carriageways, fencing, etc. Putney Vale Cemetery. Avenue, Putney Vale. 105. The growth of the shrubs in the Avenue at the entrance to Putney Vale Cemetery appeared to be affected by the adjoining trees, and some of the shrubs died. As the avenue is considered to be a very fine one the Council were anxious to preserve its appearance, and asked the London County Council to allow the Chief Officer of the Parks and Open Spaces Department to advise the Council as to dealing with the trees and shrubs. This request was acceded to, and the works suggested by the Chief Officer are being carried out under the supervision of the Borough Engineer. 106. The memorial to the Huguenots, referred to in the last report (p. 65), has been erected in the Huguenot Burial Ground, East Hill, and was unveiled on the 21st October, 1911, when the Mayor, on behalf of the Council, took charge of the memorial. I) Huguenot Burial Ground. 56 107. During the year notice was received of the intention of the London County Council to acquire property at the corner of St. Ann's Hill and Allfarthing Lane, Fairfield, as a site for a new public elementary school; and the Managers of the St. Mary's Roman Catholic Boys' School, St. Alphonsus Road, Clapham, gave notice of their proposal to enlarge the school by providing additional accommodation for about 120 children. The Borough Council did not offer any objection to either of these proposals. New Schools. 108. The County Council has also found it necessary to erect a new school at Balham, and selected property in Byrne Road and Cornford Grove as a site for the school. There was considerable opposition to this site, and the County Council eventually decided not to proceed with the acquisition thereof, but to purchase the premises Nos. 191, 193 and 195, Balham High Road. The latter site adjoins premises acquired by this Council as a site for public baths, and the County Council approached this Council with a view to an exchange of lands, allowance being made for the respective differences in value. This would have enabled the baths to be erected on the main road, and the school at the rear. This Council, however, did not entertain the proposed exchange as it would have involved them in considerable additional expenditure. A deputation waited upon the Borough Council in opposition to the Balham High Road site, and after considering the representations made, the County Council were requested to receive a deputation from the Borough Council with reference to the approaches and exits to and from the proposed school. It was also pointed out to the County Council that a site on the County Council's own land in Marius Road would be more suitable than any site previously suggested. 109. The subject of the limited powers and duties of school managers has again received consideration, together with resolutions passed by several of the other Borough Councils, and communications have been addressed to the County Council in favour of additional powers being granted. The Council was informed in reply that the appropriate Committee of the County Council regretted that they were not able to recommend any alteration in the duties at present. Powers and duties of Managers. 57 no. Three temporary schools—Camborne Road, Southfield ; Magdalen Road, Springfield ; and The Furzedown, Streatham, have been added for the purposes of management to adjoining groups of schools. In the latter case the additional school necessitated the increase of the number of Managers of the group from twelve to eighteen. Management of Schools. 111. The Aristotle Road (Boys and Girls) School, Clapham, and The Elliott (Mixed) School, Southfield, were duly constituted Central Schools under the scheme referred to in the last annual report (page 61), and the Council were informed that a commercial bias had been approved for the curriculum of such schools. The scheme provided for the withdrawal of the schools from the groups to which they formerly belonged, and the appointment of a separate body of Managers. This part of the scheme was carried out so far as this Council was concerned, but the County Council then stated that they had found it necessary to review the whole question of management, and had decided to reinstate the central schools in the groups to which they had been attached. The Council concurred in this proposal, and the two schools were accordingly reinstated. A special committee, consisting of one manager in respect of each of the contributory schools, has however been set up for each central school, to deal with the admission of pupils and the award of junior county exhibitions. Central Schools. 112. On the invitation of the Association of Representative Managers of London County Council elementary schools the Council appointed Councillor Couzens, the Chairman of the Education Committee, an honorary member of such Association. Association of Representative Managers. 113. The Council decided to concur in the views of the Wandsworth Ratepayers' Association that the regulations for the award of junior county scholarships should be amended so that children not in attendance at public elementary schools could compete on the same terms as those applicable to children who are in attendance at such schools. In the case of the former the parents' income must not exceed £160, while there is no limit in the case of children attending public elementary schools. A communication was addressed to the County Council in the matter, but they did not see their way to make any alteration in the regulations. By arrangement with the Road Board a portion of Kingston Road, from the Borough boundary to Old Portsmouth Road, has been re-surfaced, as an experiment, with various binding materials. The total cost of the work was £1,946, of which the Road Board contributed £1,447. The following is a description of the various materials laid, viz. : — Section No. 1 consists of tarred slag laid in two layers, the first graded from 2½ inches down to 1½ inches, and the second from 1½ inches to ½ inch, the surface being finished with fine uncoated chippings, making a total thickness of 4 inches. The area of this section is 1,629 square yards. It was laid by Messrs. Constable, Hart & Co., Ltd., at the contract price of 4s. per super, yard, plus a maintenance charge of 2d. per super, yard per annum for two years. Section No. 2, by Tarmac, Ltd., also consists of tarred slag, but is made up of three layers, the first graded from 21 inches to 1½ inches, the second from 1½ inches to ½ inch, and the third composed of fine topping, with a surface dressing of slag dust, the whole constituting a finished thickness of 4 inches. In area this section is 1,900 square yards, and the contract price was 3s. 10½d. per super, yard for construction, with an additional charge for maintenance at the rate of 1½d. per super, yard per annum for three years, to include painting with tar each year. Section No. 3, by Taroads Syndicate, Ltd., consists of Guernsey granite coated at the roadside with special bituminous composition 14 days before being spread. It is laid in two layers, the first graded from 2½ inches to ½ inch, and the second 3/8 inch topping dressed with fine uncoated chippings. The G 2 106 finished thickness is 3 inches, and the contract price of 3s. 4d. per super, yard carries with it a guarantee for three years without additional cost, the area of the section being 1,963 square yards. Section No. 4, by Taroads Syndicate, Ltd., also consists of Guernsey granite coated at the roadside with special bituminous composition. It is laid in two layers, the first graded from 2½ inches to ½ inch, and the second f inch topping finished with fine uncoated chippings. The tar used was slightly more viscous than the Road Board Specification No. 2. Taroads combined heater and mixer was employed for the purpose, the stone being heated previous to the coating process, then transported in barrows, spread and rolled down whilst hot to the specified thickness of 3 inches. The area of this Section is 1,757 square yards, the contract price of 3s. 2d. per super, yard covering a guarantee for three years without additional cost. Section No. 5, by Taroads Syndicate, Ltd., represents the double pitch grouting method of construction, to the Road Board specification, in three layers, the first of 2½ inches stone, the second of 1½ inches stone, and the third of ¾ inch Guernsey granite, each layer being grouted with hot "Pitchmac" and sand, and the top dressed with 3/8 inch uncoated chippings, making a finished thickness of 4 inches. Having an area of 2,006 square yards, this is the largest of the five sections. The contract price was 5s. 6d. per super, yard, but it must be taken into account that the work is guaranteed for four years without additional cost. 107 STATISTICS OF TRAFFIC taken at the Borough Boundary, Kingston Vale, from June 10th to 16th, 1911, inclusive—Road Width, 10.3 yards. Eighteen sewer ventilating shafts have been fixed against sides of houses and three columns erected during the year in lieu of surface ventilators in the roads. The total number of ventilating shafts and columns in the Borough are as follows, viz.:— 408 6-inch by 4-inch ventilating shafts. 1 4-inch by 4-inch do. 2 4-inch by 3 inch do. 82 6-inch circular do. 71 5-inch do. do. 64 4-inch do. do. 3 3-inch do. do. 140 6-inch ventilating columns 771 114 SANITARY CONVENIENCES. A new Underground Convenience for men and women has been constructed in Buckhold Road at the junction of High Street, Wandsworth. The accommodation provided is three W.C.s, eight urinal stalls, lavatory compartment and attendant's room for men, and five W.C.s, including one free W.C., lavatory compartment and attendant's room for women. The work was carried out under contract by Mr. H. Hann, the total cost, including diversion of 3-ft. 6-in. x 2 ft. 6-in. brick sewer, being £ 1,987 2s. 9d. In connection with the construction of the new tramways in Putney Bridge Road, the circular iron urinal near High Street, Wandsworth, has been removed and re-erected in Point Pleasant near the railway bridge. The work was carried out by and at the cost of the London County Council. New "Victorite" treads have been fixed 011 the steps at the Underground Convenience, Tooting Broadway, by the Patent Victoria Stone Co., at a cost of £13 6s. od. The following is a return of the receipts during the year at each of the conveniences:— £ s. d. A saving of £177 :18 : 0 has been made since December, 1910, owing to a reduction in the price of gas of 1d. per 1,000 c. feet, and of £108 :14 : 4 owing to the lighting hours being reduced from 4,300 to 4,200 per annum.— Total £286 :12 : 4. No. 3 43 4,300 123 1 9 r 4,200 127 18 6 Both No. 3 and No. 4 burners to be converted free of cost into inverted burners; contract to be for five years; lighting hours to be reduced to 4,200 per annum. Cannot offer any reduction in the present price for so short a period. Have already entered into Contracts with other Councils upon similar terms and think the substantial terms offered worthy of consideration. A saving of £4 :19 : 2 per annum can be made if the lighting hours are reduced from 4,300 hours to 4,200 hours per annum and upright burners retained. That the existing arrangements be continued for the present, except that the lighting hours be reduced from 4,300 to 4,200 per annum, so as to make the number of hours practically uniform throughout the Borough. General Report on Testings of Gas supplied to the Wandsworth Borough (i) by the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company; (2) by the Mitcham and Wimbledon Gas Company during the Year ended 31ST March, 1912. Wandsworth and Putney Qas Company. In my last annual report (iqio-ii) I referred to the installation Recent Legis'ation and Calorific Power. of a new burner in the Photometer at Disraeli Road, Putney, and to the circumstances which led to it. This new burner is known as the Metropolitan Argand Burner iNo. 2 and has the advantage of being in general use at all the Metropolitan and many provincial gas-testing places. All illuminating power tests during this year ended 31st March, 1912, have been made with the new burner, and the results obtained are therefore entirely comparable with tests made at most gas-testing places in England. At the time the new burner was introduced I again urged the institution of tests of the calorific power of the gas, and the Council having agreed to the suggestion, the Company duly provided a calorimeter and other necessary apparatus, and the tests have been made regularly since September, 1911. I had frequently pointed out, not only in my report of 1910-11 but in many previous reports, that it was of great importance to make these tests for information so as to be able to arrive at a calorific standard applicable to the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company's gas, and so that, in the event of later legislation, a standard calorific power, like the standard illuminating power, might also be set up, or even substituted for this latter. Among the many arguments in favour of this new departure, which I have put forward from time to time in various reports to the Council, I may briefly recapitulate the following:—(1) The increasing use of gas for heating and cooking purposes, and also for motor power, in addition to lighting; (2) further, its extended 1 136 use in incandescent burners, in which a non-luminous hot flame is required; (3) the greater scientific value of the calorific power as a standard of quality of gas as compared with the illuminating power standard, which long experience has shown to be in many respects uncertain and unsatisfactory. All these and other considerations make the general adoption of the calorific power as a standard of quality a practical certainty in the near future. It is with genuine gratification that I am able to refer in this present Annual Report to the final accomplishment of this desirable end and to some other distinct advances in connection with the testings of gas supplied to the Borough. On December, 1911, I received from Mr. H. G. Hills, the late Town Clerk, a copy of the Wandsworth, Wimbledon and Epsom District Gas Bill, and at his request sent a detailed report on the same, dated January 24th, 1912, which was printed. In that report I called attention to various matters connected with the testing of the gas in which change or reform had long been urgent. The most important points raised may be briefly summarised as follows:—(1) The setting up of a standard calorific power, based on the tests for information which I had made for some months previously. (2) The abolition of fixed times for testing. These hitherto had been restricted to certain hours after sunset under the Gas Works Clauses Act, 1871, an act which was passed over forty years ago, at a time when the illuminating power was apparently the only special value attaching to gas, other applications not having then been contemplated. (3) Uniform testing at all testing places in the district covered by the amalgamated gas companies. After various consultations with the gas companies, in some of which I took part, the Council succeeded in amending the Bill to their satisfaction without formally presenting a petition against it, and it has now, in the amended form, passed through both Houses of Parliament. The Wandsworth, Wimbledon and Epsom District Gas Act, 1912, comes into operation on January 1st, 1913, and I may now note the coming changes in the testing of the gas, to which I have briefly referred above. 137 In the first place the testings will be uniform throughout the District, that is to say, at all testing places the same tests will be made, viz., calorific power, illuminating power, and sulphur, in addition to sulphuretted hydrogen, and pressure observations, and there will no longer be any fixed hours of testing. The illuminating power standard will be 14 candles (section 57), and it is proposed to use, instead of the candle balance, which is antiquated, Harcourt's 10-candle Pentane lamp as the standard light in the photometer (section 59). The testing places will be the same as the existing ones, but provision is made for an additional testing place in the Wandsworth limits in accordance with a previous arrangement (sections 58 and 65). The pressure still remains at the absurdly low minimum of eighth-tenths of one inch, but there is no danger of this limit being reached, as a much greater pressure is required for the supply of gas (section 60). Testing for sulphur and sulphuretted hydrogen remain as before (section 64). There will be no penalties in connection with the above testings. The Calorific Power* (section 61).—The new calorific power standard has been fixed at 136 calories gross, with a margin of about 10 per cent., the minimum being 122 calories gross. If there is a deficiency on this minimum, the Company is liable to penalties, which increase with the deficiency. It will be noted that gross calorific values have been selected as the standard, and this has been done with the complete acquiescence of the Company. *Calorific Power.—By a calorie is meant the amount of heat required to raise the temperature of 1 kilogramme of water 1 degree Centigrade. For example, a standard of "125 Calories" would mean that the amount of heat produced by the burning of 1 cubic foot of gas (measured at 60 degrees Fahrenheit and 30 inches Barometer) must be such as to raise the temperature of 125 kilogrammes of water 1 degree Centigrade, or, taking British Units, 496 lbs. (500 lbs. nearly) of water 1 degree Fahrenheit. The net calorific power is obtained by subtracting the heat due to the condensation of some of the steam formed in the calorimeter and to the cooling of the resulting condensed water from the total observed heat or gross calorific power. In practice tl e water is measured, not weighed, hence, for practical purposes, 1 litre might be substituted for 1 kilogramme. 12 138 This will be the first Act of Parliament in which a gross calorific power standard has been set up. My reasons for advising it are:— (i) In determining the gross calorific power there is less liability to variation due to experimental error or to temporary defects of the calorimeter, and therefore less liability to dispute in case of a deficiency being found. (2) Except technically there is no difference in the gross calorific standard thus set up to a net calorific standard, since the net calorific standard originally proposed has been translated into gross value. (3) The gas referees lay no special stress on the net calorific value, as the following extract from their "Notification for the Year 191 " will show:— "The heating or calorific power of any sample of gas is represented by the number of calories produced by the combustion of one cubic foot of such gas measured at 60 deg. Fahr. and under a pressure of 30 inches of mercury. The maximum calorific power which gas can thus exert is determined directly by the calorimeter. This is a true measure of the total heating power, and is termed the gross calorific power of the gas. But in many cases in which gas is used as a heating agent, the steam which is formed escapes into the air uncondensed, and thus the heat due to the condensation of the steam and the cooling of the water so formed is not utilised. The amount of heat thus lost can be estimated, and if it is subtracted from the total heat yielded by the combustion of the gas in the calorimeter another value is obtained which is termed the net calorific power of the gas. Since, however, when steam escapes uncondensed, the uncondensable products of combustion also pass away at a high temperature, and since the loss of heat thus arising is commonly the greater of the two, the customary partial correction from gross to net has not much significance." Finally, I may state that the standard calorific power agreed upon has been arrived at from a careful consideration of the tests of calorific power of the gas which I made between October 3rd, 1911, and January 12th, 1912, which yielded an average of 135*3 gross calories (see Report dated January 24th, 1912, above referred to). Inasmuch as tests for illuminating power were invariably made by me at the same time, and average about I5'0 candles, this illuminating power may be said to approximately correspond to a calorific power of about 135 gross calories, but I shall refer to these details later. Usual Tests made during 1911-12. Table I. shows the average illuminating power for each month Illuminating Power. of the annual period, viz., from April, 1911, to March, 1912. From this table it will be seen that the total average for the year ended 31st March, 1912, was 15.1 candles, the minimum being 147 (April and November, 1911, and February, 1912), the maximum being I5.5 (July, 1911). Table III. shows the curve representing weekly variations during the same period, with a minimum weekly average of 14.1 (February, 1912), and a maximum weekly average of 16.1 (September, 1911). In no case has the illuminating power been below 14-0 candles, the statutory limit. The general average is somewhat higher than during the last three years, but, as will be seen from the curve in Table III., there has also been some considerable fluctuation. As noted under "Recent Legislation " in the foregoing pages, Calorific Power. caionnc power tests for lniormation were commenced in September, 1911. During September the results obtained were not very satisfactory, and were partly, without doubt, due to some defects in the calorimeter, newly set up at the time, and which had not been thoroughly adjusted. From October, 1911, to March, 1912, fairly even results were obtained, as will be seen from Table I., in which the monthly averages are shown, and from Table III., which shows the curve of the weekly averages of calorific power determinations. From an inspection of Table I. it will be noted that the general average for the six months ended 31st March, 1912, was 1347 gross calories and 120.9 net, with a maximum monthly average of 136.4 140 gross calories and 121.7 net calories in December, 191 r, and ar minimum, monthly average of I33.1 gross and 120.1 net calories in February, 1912. The weekly averages indicated by the curve in Table III. show that the extreme variation during this same period was not excessive, the minimum being 132 gross calories (November and December, 1911, and February, 1912), and the maximum 141.0 gross calories (March, 1912). The question has, I am aware, been frequently asked as to what is the relation between the illuminating power and the calorific power. So far as general experience goes, at present there does not appear to be any definite relation such as would enable an observer to calculate the one from the other. There are many obvious reasons for this absence of definite relationship. On the other hand, experience has also shown that, as a rule,high illuminating power corresponds to a high calorific power, and this somewhat general deduction is more or less demonstrated on comparing the curves shown in Table III. I have also shown, in Table I., the monthly averages of sulphur Sulphur. (grains in lou cuuic ieet; ior uie year enueu jisi March, 1912. In Table III. the curve of weekly averages is shown, and here the minimum is 12 grains, in February, 1912, and the maximum nearly 33 grains, in April, 1911. I—« 00 183 Appendix "F." REPORT OF THE WANDSWORTH DISTRESS COMMITTEE. From 1st July, 1911, to 30th June, 1912. Appointment. The Distress Committee was appointed by the Borough Council on the nth October, 1905, in accordance with the Unemployed Workmen Act (1905), and constituted as follows :— Members of the Borough Council 12 Members of the Board of Guardians 8 Persons experienced in the relief of distress 5 Members of Committee. Members of the Council :—Aldermen Cresswell, Hewett, Lorden, Penfold, and Robinson ; Councillors Anderson, Couzens, Denny, Everett, Jackson, Plumridge and Prince. Members of the Board of Guardians :—Rev. J. Cooney, Mr. G. J. Fowle, Mr. W. P. Melhuish, Mr. E. A. Miller, m.b., Mr. Percivai Rees (Chairman), Lieut. E. A. Sanders, r.n., and Mr. A. Sullivan (one vacancy). Members experienced in the relief of distress, appointed for one year :—Rev. D. Tudor Craig, Mr. A. O. Groves, Miss M. H. Pollock and Mr. C. A. Upton (one vacancy). m 184 Sub.Committee and reference. A Sub.Committee of twelve members was formed constituted as follows :—Mr. Percival Rees (Chairman) ; Alderman Cresswell, Councillors Anderson, Couzens, Denny and Jackson ; Lieut. Sanders, R.v, Rev. J. Cooney, Mr. G. J. Fowle, Mr. C. A. Upton, Miss M. H. Pollock (one vacancy), and "the Chairman and Members of the Central Body ex.officio : the duties being to enquire and report as to the condition of labour, to consider and classify the Record Papers when completed. There has been no change from the methods adopted in previous years in the matters of reception at office, investigation of cases, and selection of cases recommended for work, migration and emigration. Representatives of Wandsworth on the Central (Unemployed) Body of London. Rev. J. H. Anderson, m.a., Chairman of the Central Body, and Chairman of Works Committee. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Central Body, 100 00 per cent. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Works Committee, 80 00 per cent. As ex.officio member, attended meetings of other Standing Committees and Sub.Committees on 41 occasions. Mr. Percival Rees, Chairman of Finance Sub.Committee of Accounts, Chairman of Finance Committee up to 20th October, 1911. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Central Body, 87 5 per cent. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Finance Sub.Committee of Accounts, 80.oo per cent. 185 ATTENDANCE OF COMMITTEE.
