Ice Cream Premises. At the end of 1910 there were 287 of these on the Register. During 1911 42 were added and 25 removed, leaving a total of 304 on the Register. 480 inspections were made of these premises during the year and 53 notices were served, all of which were for cleansing. Houses Let in Lodgings. At the end of 1910 there were 292 houses let in lodgings on the Register. None were added during 1911 and none removed, making a total of 292 on the Register at the end of iqit. 721 inspections of these were made during the year, and 637 notices were served, 68 for overcrowding and 569 for other conditions, chiefly cleansing. With regard to four premises summonses were issued for failing to cleanse and for other nuisances, and convictions were obtained in each case. 220 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. On the whole the By-laws have been satisfactorily complied with, although in some instances the cleansing was not carried out at the specified time. The question of making an alteration in the present By-laws so as to conform with the Housing, Town Planning, etc., Act, 1909, has been carefully considered by the Council, but it was not considered necessary to make any alteration at present as the Solicitor was of opinion that the By-laws were in compliance with that Act. Offensive Trade Refuse. The arrangements which have been made by the Council with a contractor for the removal of this refuse have during the year worked quite satisfactorily, and no complaints have been received. In a certain number of cases this refuse is removed privately, and this has also been carried out ir a satisfactory manner. Unsound Food. During the year two trunks of Soles, one box of Hake, one box of Whiting, one box of Herrings, one box of Skate, one trunk of Mackerel, 250 Eggs, two barrels of Apples, four trays of Pears, two baskets of Mushrooms, and one bag of Walnuts, were destroyed at the request of the owners, and the usual certificates granted. Factories and Workshops. Although there has been a decrease in the total number of inspections of the above, compared with 1910, yet an examination of the Tables will show that a very large amount of work has been done. Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 221 As has been stated in this Report when dealing with Infective Diseases the Inspectors had a very large increase of cases to deal with, and this consequently lessened the time that could be devoted to inspections of factories and workshops. I have also this year visited a large number of these premises and am able to report that they are all in a very satisfactory condition. The fact that no prosecution was necessary to abate any nuisances found shows that there has been no difficulty in carrying out the provisions of the Act. With regard to outworkers it has again been found necessary, as a matter of routine, to forward a warning letter to the majority of employers. The Tables Vvhich follow are similar to those used in previous Reports, and the whole of the work done by both male and female Inspectors is there shown in a concise form. The total number of workshops on the Register was 1,690 including 128 retail bakehouses, 144 workshop laundries, 286 dressmakers' and milliners' premises, and 1,132 other workshops, but not including 374 factories, 1,094 workplaces, and 312 outworkers' premises. Including all factories, workshops, workplaces, and outworkers' premises, there were on the Register at the end of 1911 3,470 premises, compared with 3,420 in 1910, 3,305 in 1909, 3,347 in 1908, 3,281 in 1907, and 3,096 in 1906. The total number of inspections made during the year was 6,050, compared with 6,387 in 1910, 6,531 in 1909, 5,801 in 1908, 6,048 in 1907, and 5,997 in 1906. The total number of notices served was 462, 429 intimation and 33 statutory, compared with 580 in 1910, 597 in 1909, 434 in 1908, 453 in 1907, and 427 in 1906. 222 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. There were no prosecutions under the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, during the year. Under the head of other workshops are included domestic workshops, and under the head of places where food is prepared for sale are included the kitchens of hotels, restaurants, tripe, fried fish and eel shops, and other places where food is prepared for sale. In all 708 inspections were made of 374 factories, and 52 notices, 50 intimation and two statutory, were served. The total number of the workshops on the Register was 1,690, 144 of which were workshop laundries, 128 workshop bakehouses, and 1,418 other workshops. In all 3,059 inspections of these were made, compared with 3,346 in 1910, 3,366 in 1909, 3.130 in 1908, 3,148 in 1907, 3,233 in 1906, and 2,628 in 1905, and 195 intimation and 15 statutory notices were served. The total number of workplaces on the Register was 1,094 and 1,879 inspections were made, while 157 intimation and 14 statutory notices were served. The total number of defects found was 614, including 13 cases in which there was a breach of special sanitary requirements for bakehouses compared with 720 and 11 in 1910. To abate these nuisances 429 intimation and 33 statutory notices were served, all of which, with the exception of 15, were complied with at the end of the year. The 15 outstanding were complied with in the first month of this year. Excluding outworkers' premises 614 defects were found and 599 remedied, but only 402 intimation notices were served, as one notice frequently called attention to several defects on the same premises. At the end of 1910 there were 314 outworkers' premises on the Register, 32 were added and 34 removed during the year, leaving 312 on the Register. 404 inspections were made of these premises during the year, and 29 notices, all for cleansing, were served and complied with. Statement of Work done under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts. During the past year 927 samples of foods and drugs were submitted to the Public Analyst for analysis, compared with 1,030 in 1909, 1,004 i'1 1908, 989 in 1907, and 905 in 1906. Of these 123 or 13.2 per cent. were reported to be adulterated, compared with 9*05 per cent, in 1910, 6.89 per cent. in 1909, 876 per cent. in 1908, 8.49 per cent. in 1907, and 9.29 per cent. in 1906. The percentage of milk samples found to be adulterated was 9.3, compared with 7.44 in 1910, 7.39 in 1909, 6.9 in 1908, and 10.97 in 1907. In 17 of the adulterated milk samples the Public Health Committee, after considering the amount of adulteration and the circumstances of the sale, decided not to prosecute the vendor, so that the percentages of prosecutions was 6.33, compared with 3.9 in 1910, 4 in 1909, 3.8 in 1908, and 5.9 in 1907. In 77 out of the 123 cases in which adulterations were detected proceedings were instituted against the vendor, compared with 55 in 1910, 44 in 1909, and 50 in 1908. The total amount received in penalties under the above Acts during the year amounted to £244 12s. od., and the costs to £55 7s. 6d., making a total of £299 19s. 6d., compared with £154 us. 0d. in 1910, and £92 5s. od. in 1909. A penalty of 40s. was inflicted on one vendor for an assault on an agent employed by the Inspector, with 12s. costs, and a penalty of £4 was inflicted on another vendor under the Merchandise Marks Acts for selling washing soda adulterated with Glauber's Salt, with £2 2s. od. costs, making a total of £8 14s. od., and a grand total of £308 13s. 6d. 240 Report of the Medical Officer oj Health. From this table it will be seen that the average percentage of adulterations detected for the 10 years 1901-10 was 9 2 per cent., compared with 13-2 in 1911, an increase of no less than 4 per cent. This increase is partly due to the large amount of adulteration detected in milk and butter samples. There are also other factors which have a direct bearing on this increase, the chief being that the Inspector has made a determined effort to follow up the habitually fraudulent trader, with the result that no less than twenty of these, who had been convicted several times and in some cases imprisoned, have left the Borough. 246 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Milk and Cream. MILK. 586 samples of milk were procured during the year. 55, or 93 per cent. were found to be adulterated, of which 25 or 463 per cent. were deficient in original milk fat, and 24 or 43.6 per cent. were found to contain added water, three samples were both deficient in milk fat and contained added water, and in four samples preservatives were detected. In 37 cases proceedings were taken against the vendor of the adulterated sample, and penalties amounting to £101 5s. od. were inflicted, with costs amounting to £26 12s. od., the penalties ranging from 5s. to £20 with costs. 23 samples of milk were procured on delivery at Public Institutions situated within the Borough and only one sample was reported against. Proceedings were taken against the milk contractor supplying the milk, who however, successfully pleaded a warranty. 24 samples of milk were procured whilst in course of delivery at various Railway Stations within the Borough, this milk being consigned from farmers in the country to retailers within the Borough, and in every case the sample was well above the standard. 12 samples of milk were taken whilst in course of transit, or on delivery from the wholesale dairy companies to the retailer and in each case the milk was of good quality. 17 samples of milk were procured on delivery at private houses, of which 9 or 53 per cent. were found to be adulterated. Proceedings were taken against seven of the vendors and convictions obtained in each case. 249 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Private Houses 17 9 53 157 samples of milk have been taken on Sundays either in the early morning or at mid-day. 17, or 10 per cent. were reported against as being adulterated. Proceedings were taken against 11 of the vendors with the result that convictions were obtained in each case. 310 samples of milk were procured during the early mornings on week days. Of these 36 or 11.2 per cent. were found to be adulterated. Proceedings were taken in 21 cases and convictions obtained. In five cases proceedings were taken against the vendors for selling milk from a receptacle upon which their name and address were not conspicuously inscribed. Four of these were convicted, while one absconded before service of summons. I am pleased to report that in no case during the year has the inspector been obstructed in the course of his duty and no "refusal to sell" a sample for analysis has taken place. 250 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. In nine cases the defendants relied on a warranty, but in four cases only were the defendants able to satisfy the Magistrate that the milk was sold in the same condition as received. In 10 cases the Public Health Committee alter considering the various circumstances, such as conditions of sale and the amount of preservative, decided not to prosecute but to caution the vendors. In two cases proceedings were instituted against the vendors. In one instance the vendor was find £3 and costs and in the second case the summons was withdrawn owing to the reserve sample having burst. Butter and Margarine. BUTTER. 189 samples of butter were analysed by the Public Analyst during the year of which 31 or 16.4 per cent. were reported against, compared with 7.23 per cent. in 1910 and 5.35 per cent. in 1909, thus showing a very great increase. Here again the Inspector has made a vigorous effort to follow up the fraudulent trader. In two instances during the year the trader was not deterred by his first conviction, but continued to pursue his practice of substituting margarine when butter was demanded by the purchaser, and in these cases second and third convictions weie obtained. In 31 cases proceedings were instituted against the vendors and convictions obtained. The total amount of penalties including costs received amounted to £113 4s. od., these penalties ranging from £1 to £25 and costs. It is satisfactory to report that of all the butter samples examined not one was found to contain any excess of moisture or preservative. Six samples of butter were purchased from butter hawkers and four of the six were adulterated. These men go from door to door in some of the best parts of the Borough and represent that "25- Repori of the Medical Officer of Health. they are farmers selling their own dairy produce. This so-called butter sold at from is. id. to is. 4d. per lb. proved to be entirely margarine, probably worth about 4d. or 5d. per lb., and is usually done up in every way to represent dairy butter, with the impression of a cow or other object stamped on the top. These men are usually very difficult to catch, being provided with a pony and trap, and they move very quickly from district to district never returning at regular intervals. The Inspector reports that he has waited whole days in districts where these men are known to sell their goods, without result. The Inspector was successful in catching two of these traders during the year, and in one case the defendant was find £3 4s. od., and in the other £5 and £2 3s. 6d. costs. Within two months of this last mentioned conviction the vendor was seen by the Inspector trading in an adjoining Borough. Information was at once given to the Inspector of that Borough with the result that the vendor was still found to be carrying on his dishonest business. Proceedings were again taken against him with the result that he was convicted and fined £14 and £2 17s. 6d. costs. Much valuable information has been received from the Food Inspectors of neighbouring Boroughs concerning traders, especially itinerant milk vendors and butter hawkers, and the Inspector has likewise given information and assisted by giving evidence at Police Courts for Inspectors of adjoining Boroughs. The following Table shows the number of butter samples taken, the number found adulterated, and the percentage of adulteration, together with the average adulteration for the years 1901-10, compared with the year under review. 253 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. TABLE CXVI. Year. Number of samples taken. Number Adulterated. Five samples of margarine were submitted for analysis, one of which was reported against. There were four convictions in connection with the sale of margarine, one for exposing margarine for sale without having it properly labelled, and three for selling margarine in an unstamped wrapper, the fines and costs inflicted amounting to £6 10s. 0d. 254 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Cheese. Two samples of cheese were submitted for analysis and in both cases were returned as genuine. The Inspector reports that the sale of gorgonzola cheese, particulars of which were given in the Report for 1910, has been discontinued, for in no case during the year has any of this article been seen exposed for sale, the Inspector keeping a sharp look out during his many visits to shops in the Borough. Lard. Three samples of lard were submitted for analysis and all three were returned as genuine. Bread. One sample of standard bread was analysed and proved to be genuine. Flour. During the year under review the Local Government Board issued a report on the presence of calcium sulphate in baking powders and self-raising flour. The report, which was by Dr. J. M. Hamill, recommended certain limits of calcium sulphate in baking powders and self-raising flour. The Inspector was therefore instructed to procure samples and two samples of self-raising flour and nine samples of baking powder were examined, and one of flour and one of baking powder were found to contain an excess of calcium sulphate. The following circular was then issued, and a copy sent to all traders who sold baking powders or self-raising flour. "The attention of the Wandsworth Borough Council has beer called to the large amount of Calcium Sulphate in some samples of Baking Powder and Self-Raising Flour which have been submitted to the Public Analyst. 255 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. "The Council desires to point out that the 'Acid Phosphate' used in the preparation of these articles should not contain more than 10 per cent, of Calcium Sulphate, and hereby gives notice that the question of taking proceedings under the Sale of Food and Drugs Act will be considered in any cases in which it is found that the amount of Calcium Sulphate in the Phosphate employed in making such Baking Powder or Self-Raising Flour exceeds the above percentage. HENRY GEORGE HILLS, Town Clerk. Council House, Wandsworth, S.W. May, ign." Coffee. 10 samples of coffee were procured for analysis, one sample having been reported as adulterated. Proceedings were taken against the vendor, who was fined £2 and costs. Coffee Mixtures. Seven samples of coffee and chicory were analysed, in six the proportion of coffee and chicory was about equal, in one case reported against the Public Analyst stated that the sample contained 93 per cent. of chicory and seven per cent, of coffee. Proceedings were taken against the vendor, who at the hearing of the summons requested that the reserve sample be analysed by the Government Analyst, who subsequently stated that in his opinion the sample was genuine, the proportion of coffee and chicory being about equal, the summons was therefore withdrawn. Cocoa. Six samples of cocoa were submitted for analysis and all were returned fis genuine. 256 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Sugar. 10 samples of sugar were analysed, one of which was reported against. This sample was purchased as Demerara sugar, but on analysis proved to be dyed or coloured crystals. In this case the vendor was cautioned. Drugs. 10 samples of drugs, which included two prescriptions, were taken and one sample was reported against. This was a sample of Gregory's powder which was not prepared in accordance with the requirements of the British Pharmacepoeia. No action was taken against the vendor in this case, as the adulteration was not a serious one, being the substitution of magnesium carbonate for magnesium oxide. Other Articles. 77 samples classified under this heading were procured for analysis, and 20 or 25-9 per cent, were reported against. The chief adulterations occurred in the tinned or canned foods, in which a small amount of metallic contamination was detected, but in no case was the amount considered injurious to health. 12 samples of rice were analysed, all of which were reported to be free from "facing." 12 samples of sausage and prepared meats were analysed for preservatives, and it is very satisfactory to state that 10 of the samples were found to be entirely free from preservatives, whilst the two cases reported against contained only a very small amount of preservative. A comparison of this year's percentage of 16.6 against that for 1910, which was 58, shows that the proceedings which were very reluctantly taken against several vendors for adding an excessive amount of preservative to prepared meats, have done a great deal of good in checking this form of adulteration. 257 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Six samples of common washing soda were analysed, but as this article was not a food or a drag, it was necessary to procure the samples, and take proceedings under the Merchandise Marks Act. Two samples were reported as being adulterated with sulphate of soda or what is known as Glauber's salts, this salt being about one half the price of ordinary washing soda. Glauber's salt is useless for the purpose for which washing soda is used, in fact, the percentage found in the samples quite neutralised the softening effect of the genuine soda with which it was mixed. Proceedings were taken against the vendors of the two samples reported against as being adulterated. The first case heard resulted in a conviction, the defendant being fined £4 and £2 2s. 0d. costs. The Inspector appointed to carry out the work under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts has done admirable work during the year and has been the means of stopping certain forms of adulteration which were prevalent and which were extremely difficult to discover. The year 1911 was an exceptionally busy one, not only as regards the executive duties of the staff, but also as regards the clerical work. The exceptional prevalence of Measles, Whooping Cough and Diarrhoea, as well as the new duties which devolved on the staff with regard to Pulmonary Tuberculosis largely increased the work, but I am pleased to be able to report that it has all been carried out in a most satisfactory manner. I have the honour to be, Mr. Mayor and Gentlemen, Your obedient servant, P. CALDWELL SMITH, I Medical Officer of Health. ANNUAL STATEMENT Of the work done in the Borough of Wandsworth under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts, summarised from the statutoryquarterly reports. To the Mayor, Aldermen and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth. Sir and Gentlemen, In presenting the Annual Statement of the work done under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts, during the year 1911, it is in the fisrt place my sad duty to record the death of the Public Analyst, my father, Dr. John Muter, which occurred on December 19th. From that date to the end of the year the work has been carried on by me, and it is in my capacity as Public Analyst to the Borough for the first three months of the present year that I have prepared this statement The total number of samples submitted by the Inspector Number of samples submitted. during tne year amounted to 927. Of these, 919 were taken with the formalities required by the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts; six were taken under the Merchandise Marks Act, whilst the remaining two were procured informally. It is a noteworthy fact that both these informal samples were "Informal samples. iound to be adulterated, tne nrst, sold as butter, proving to be entirely margarine; the second bought as milk, proving to be a mixture of 42 parts of milk with 58 parts of water. Incidentally, this sample provided the most gross case of adulteration met with during the year in relation to the milk supply. The statement following gives the result of analyses of all articles submitted. Articles other than Milk, Cream, and Butter. Of the samples submitted other than milk, cream, and butter, the number amounted to 136. Of these, 25, or 183 per cent., were reported as adulterated or not up to the standard, and full details concerning these are given in Table D. The two samples included under the heading "Flour" were The presence of Calcium 8ulphatc in Baking Powder and Self-raising Flour. both "Self-raising" Flours. These, together with the nine samples of Baking Powder, were submitted on account of the publication during the year of Dr. J. M. Hamill's Report to the Local Government Board " On the presence of Calcium Sulphate in Baking Powder and Selfraising Flour." It will be seen that two only of the samples (Flour Sample No. 371 and Baking Powder Sample No. 374) were reported as containing this impurity in excess of the amount recommendcel as permissible in the Report referred to. A series of tinned goods were submitted and examined, with Metallic contamination in tinned goods. special reterence to metallic contamination, but in no case was the quantity of dissolved tin found to exceed 2'0 grains per lb. It is satisfactory to note that of the ten samples of Sausages Preservatives In Sausages. submitted, two only this year were found to contain a preservative, consisting in both instances of Boric Acid. Ten samples of " Drugs " were examined, adulteration being Drugs. reported in but one case; namely, Gregory s Powder, sample No. 119, where Magnesium Carbonate had been employed in its preparation instead of Magnesium Oxide. The six samnles referred to as beiner taken under the Washing Soda. Merchandise Marks Act consisted of Washing Soda. Of these, four proved to be genuine, and two adulterated. The latter, samples No. 510 and No. 512, were found to contain 68.69 per cent. and 45.42 per cent., respectively, crystallised sodium sulphate, an inert substance devoid of detergent properties.
